## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task involves modeling the rate of change of concentration (dA/dt) as a function of time and current concentration in a chemical reaction. This is a classic chemical kinetics problem where the rate law describes how concentration evolves, typically following nth-order kinetics, autocatalytic mechanisms, or more complex rate expressions.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- {'name': 'Zero-order kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0', 'scenario': 'Constant rate of reaction independent of concentration'}
- {'name': 'First-order kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A', 'scenario': 'Rate proportional to concentration (radioactive decay, unimolecular decomposition)'}
- {'name': 'Second-order kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A**2', 'scenario': 'Rate proportional to square of concentration (bimolecular reaction of same species)'}
- {'name': 'nth-order kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A**c1', 'scenario': 'General power-law rate dependence on concentration'}
- {'name': 'Mixed-order kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2', 'scenario': 'Parallel first and second order reaction pathways'}
- {'name': 'Reversible first-order reaction', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A + c1', 'scenario': 'First-order forward and reverse reactions approaching equilibrium'}
- {'name': 'Autocatalytic rate law', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A)', 'scenario': 'Autocatalytic reaction where product catalyzes the reaction'}
- {'name': 'Saturation kinetics (substrate inhibition)', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A + c2 * A**2)', 'scenario': 'Enzyme kinetics with substrate inhibition'}
- {'name': 'Time-dependent rate coefficient', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t) * A', 'scenario': 'Reaction with time-varying conditions (e.g., temperature ramp)'}
- {'name': 'Consecutive reaction intermediate', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t) + c2 * exp(c3 * t)', 'scenario': 'Concentration rate for intermediate species in consecutive reactions'}
- {'name': 'Power-law with offset', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2', 'scenario': 'nth-order kinetics with a constant source or sink term'}
- {'name': 'Fractional order with saturation', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (c2 + A**c1)', 'scenario': 'Generalized saturation kinetics with cooperative effects'}
- {'name': 'Polynomial rate expression', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 + c1 * A + c2 * A**2 + c3 * A**3', 'scenario': 'Empirical polynomial fit for complex multi-step mechanisms'}

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope â†’ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects â†’ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay â†’ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior â†’ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects â†’ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Negative rate (consumption) with concentration dependence â†’ dA_dt = -c * A**n with c > 0, indicating reactant depletion
- Equilibrium approach â†’ Rate expression with both positive and negative terms (e.g., c0*A + c1) indicating forward and reverse reactions
- Autocatalytic S-shaped dynamics â†’ Product of concentration and remaining capacity A*(c - A), logistic-like rate
- Concentration-only dependence (no explicit time) â†’ Autonomous ODE suggesting a closed-form rate law dA_dt = f(A)
- Explicit time dependence â†’ Non-autonomous system suggesting external forcing, time-varying temperature, or catalyst deactivation
- Half-integer or fractional reaction orders â†’ A**0.5 or A**1.5 suggesting radical chain mechanisms or surface reactions
- Rate approaching zero as Aâ†’0 â†’ Power-law A**n with n > 0, physically consistent with no reaction at zero concentration
- Inflection in rate vs concentration â†’ Rational or polynomial forms suggesting competing pathways or inhibition effects
